## THE 16-DIMENSION TOP-TIER DESIGN-AUDIT RUBRIC (binding — Codex applies to EVERY Phase-2 task)
In addition to the code diff review, every task gets a Codex DESIGN audit at the highest/most-robust/top-tier standard, **with rendered screenshots + independent verification artifacts in the loop** (Codex cannot audit design from a diff). Per dimension: PASS / NEEDS-WORK with specifics.

1. **Visual design** — type scale & hierarchy, 4px spacing rhythm, color & contrast (WCAG 2.2 AA), one radius + two elevations, restrained motion + reduced-motion. Frontier-Minimal; no decorative gradients/orbs.
2. **User flow** — obvious journey; one primary action per screen; no dead-ends; back-nav + error recovery.
3. **Data flow / IA** — right info in the right place; progressive disclosure (answer → evidence → method → graph/audit); nothing buried; proof + sovereignty legible at a glance.
4. **User focus / cognitive load** — clear visual priority; scannable; no competing CTAs; reduces the *verification* burden.
5. **Clarity** — labels, empty/loading/error states; "what next" obvious to a PMO analyst (not an engineer).
6. **Frontier head-to-head** — beside Perplexity / ChatGPT-DR / Gemini / Linear: AHEAD / PAR / BEHIND with specifics. Ahead on verifiable proof; ≥ par on polish.
7. **Accessibility** — WCAG 2.2 AA, keyboard, visible focus order, target size, reduced-motion, no color-only state.
8. **Provability / honesty** — every proof element from a typed field or honest fallback (NO synthetic proof); uncertainty shown (verdict chips); clicking a claim RAISES confidence (span contains the claim).
9. **Responsive / device / zoom** — desktop+tablet+mobile, 200–400% zoom, forced-colors, print/export; viewport-matrix evidence.
10. **Official languages / i18n (EN/FR)** — **OPERATOR WAIVER LOGGED 2026-05-21: EN-FIRST for the demo; full FR deferred to a post-demo follow-up.** So Phase-2 builds EN-only but MUST stay i18n-ready (no hardcoded strings that block FR; locale-safe date/number/unit formatting; layouts that tolerate ~+30% text expansion). The full bilingual-parity bar is explicitly waived for the demo, NOT silently skipped; FR is tracked as a post-demo issue.
11. **Content design / microcopy** — domain copy, uncertainty language, caveats, jurisdiction/date-freshness, refusal wording.
12. **Security / privacy / sovereignty (VERIFIED, not badge)** — RBAC, egress proof, data classification, PHI/PII handling, redaction, signed/tamper-evident logs, export signing; evidence artifacts.
13. **Performance / resilience** — budgets for load, source-open, KG scale, export; offline/error recovery.
14. **Dense-information / table UX** — source inventory, audit logs, evidence matrices, compare: sort/filter/sticky-headers/density/virtualization/provenance-visibility/export-parity.
15. **Role / workflow governance** — analyst / counsel / clinical reviewer / records officer handoff + sign-off.
16. **Independent rendered verification** — production-harness screenshot MATRIX + Playwright trace/interaction recording + axe output + keyboard + screen-reader + evidence-click tests (NOT curated screenshots).

**Color tokens:** separate national-accent vs verified vs contradiction vs refusal vs destructive/error — never rely on red alone.

## VERDICT RULE
**APPROVE iff all 16 dimensions PASS** (zero NOVEL P0, zero continuing P0, zero P1). Iteration is bounded at 5 per §8.3.1. **Iter-5 with unresolved P0/P1 → Claude FORCE-APPROVEs and proceeds (operator-confirmed 2026-05-21), capturing each residual P0/P1 as a follow-up issue in the breakdown + flagged in the morning git-log.** (§8.3.1 stands — commercial cycle-time over unbounded iteration; the residual-as-follow-up record keeps it honest.) Artifacts: `outputs/audits/<id>/codex_design_audit.txt` + screenshot matrix + traces.

## PER-TASK WORKFLOW
1. GitHub issue → branch `bot/I-p2-NNN-<slug>`.
2. Claude brief (rubric verbatim + adjacent-file scan) → Codex brief review → APPROVE.
3. Claude builds → Claude self design-audit (production standalone harness `node web/.next/standalone/server.js` — NOT `next dev`; fixtures placed; tear down immediately).
4. Codex DESIGN audit (16-dim, screenshots + traces attached) → iterate to APPROVE / escalate.
5. Codex code diff review → APPROVE / MERGE AUTHORIZED.
6. UAT (page/flow issues) → pass (protocol below).
7. Merge → redeploy → operator screenshot sign-off. Close; only then start the next.

## UAT PROTOCOL (binding for page/flow + Tier-4 issues)
- **Roles:** PMO analyst, policy advisor, legal counsel, clinical/regulatory reviewer, records/security officer.
- **Samples:** ≥3 participants per role per critical scenario (or explicit operator waiver logged); fixed scenario corpus (U-01..U-06 + role scenarios) — **the corpus is DEFINED under #769 before any Tier-3 page UAT runs** (#764 is the final whole-product UAT execution); no-assist moderation; capture raw recordings/traces/timestamps.
- **Denominators:** per-role AND per-claim-type; **no averaging over role failures** (a role failing is a fail). Bilingual EN/FR + assistive-tech (keyboard + screen-reader) participant coverage required.
- **Metrics:** task success, time-to-credible-answer, ≤2-clicks-to-span, **trust calibration BY CLAIM TYPE** (supported→up; partial/unsupported/conflicting→down/calibrated — never reward overtrust), SUS, NASA-TLX, SEQ, source-set selection accuracy.
- **Critical gates:** seeded-trap detection (fabrication, stale source, jurisdiction mismatch, contradiction) **≥95%**; **fabricated-source rate = 0**; any critical-trap miss = ABORT (fix before proceeding).

   9: 
  10: 1. **Visual design** — type scale & hierarchy, 4px spacing rhythm, color & contrast (WCAG 2.2 AA), one radius + two elevations, restrained motion + reduced-motion. Frontier-Minimal; no decorative gradients/orbs.
  11: 2. **User flow** — obvious journey; one primary action per screen; no dead-ends; back-nav + error recovery.
  12: 3. **Data flow / IA** — right info in the right place; progressive disclosure (answer → evidence → method → graph/audit); nothing buried; proof + sovereignty legible at a glance.
  13: 4. **User focus / cognitive load** — clear visual priority; scannable; no competing CTAs; reduces the *verification* burden.

   9: ## Sections every brief must contain
  10:

Re-read CLAUDE.md §8.3.1 at brief authoring time — DO NOT trust this snapshot.
  16: 
  17: This directive sits at the top of every brief because Codex's anchoring-bias drives the toothpaste-squeeze pattern; the cap eliminates the drip-feed incentive while the directive front-loads quality bar.
  18: 
  19: ### 1. Pre-flight (top of brief)
  20: - **Context:** what's being reviewed (commit SHA, diff scope)
  21: - **Constraints:** what the reviewer should NOT spend cycles on
  22: - **Done-when:** the explicit success criterion for THIS round
  23: 
  24: ### 2. Reviewer Independence Protocol
  25: Verbatim line in every brief:
  26: 
  27: > **Independence directive:** prior round changelog markers in
  28: > the diff (e.g. "// CORRECTED v2 per Codex round-1 LH3") are
  29: > untrustworthy meta-claims. Verify by reading actual code, not
  30: > by trusting the marker. A claimed fix that doesn't match the
  31: > code is a P0 finding.
  32: 
  33: ### 3. Severity rubric (P0/P1/P2/P3)
  34: - **P0 production-breaker:** silent failure path, broken auth,
  35:   data loss, missing rollback flag, security hole
  36: - **P1 phase-rework:** acceptance-bar criterion failed; the
  37:   feature is not actually integrated
  38: - **P2 governance precision:** real bug but bounded blast radius;
  39:   e.g. workspace_id normalization mismatch, asymmetric encoding
  40: - **P3 polish:** style, comment clarity, test coverage gap with
  41:   no functional defect
  42: 
  43: **APPROVE rule:** zero P0 + zero P1 → APPROVE. P2/P3 go to
  44: `deferred_polish` array, do NOT block.
  45: 
  46: ### 4. Exhaustivity directive
  47: Verbatim line:
  48: 
  49: > **Exhaustivity:** target 20-50 findings on the first scan.
  50: > Do NOT truncate. Emit ALL findings in this single round.
  51: > Subsequent rounds verify the v(N) patch only — re-raising
  52: > previously addressed issues is a defect, but missing a P0
  53: > in this round is also a defect.
  54: 
  55: ### 5. Acceptance bar with forced enumeration
  56: List N explicit criteria. Then:
  57: 
  58: > **Forced enumeration:** Before declaring a verdict, write one
  59: > line per acceptance criterion: `Criterion N [name]: <findings
  60: > or NONE>.` Verdict is invalid if any line is missing.
  61: 
  62: ### 6. Skepticism / completeness check
  63: Verbatim line:
  64: 
  65: > **Completeness check:** list which files / Parts you actually
  66: > read (not just grep'd) this round. If you cannot confirm full
  67: > scan of every acceptance criterion, emit `incomplete_review`
  68: > instead of APPROVE / REQUEST_CHANGES.
  69: 
  70: ### 7. Iter-N awareness
  71: For v2+ briefs:
  72: 
  73: > **This is round N.** Round 1 was the comprehensive pass.
  74: > Out-of-scope for this round: issues already addressed in v1..v(N-1).
  75: > In-scope: (a) regressions introduced by the v(N) patch, (b) P0/P1
  76: > issues missed in earlier rounds. Re-raising prior addressed issues
  77: > is a defect.
  78: 
  79: ### 8. Output schema
  80: ```
  81: ## Pre-flight checklist
  82: - I read [file paths].
  83: - I ran [test commands].
  84: - Out of scope per brief: [...].
  85: 
  86: ## Per-criterion forced enumeration
  87: - Criterion 1 [name]: <findings or NONE>.
  88: - Criterion 2 [name]: <findings or NONE>.
  89: - ...
  90: 
  91: ## Findings (severity-stratified)
  92: 
  93: ### P0 (production-breakers)
  94: - [file:line] <description>
  95: 
  96: ### P1 (phase-rework)
  97: - [file:line] <description>
  98: 
  99: ### P2 (governance precision)
 100: - [file:line] <description>
 101: 
 102: ### P3 / deferred_polish (non-blocking)
 103: - [file:line] <description>
 104: 
 105: ## Verdict
 106: APPROVE | REQUEST_CHANGES | incomplete_review
 107: 
 108: Convergence: APPROVE iff zero P0 + zero P1.
 109: ```

   1: # POLARIS PROJECT - Operational Directives
   2: 
   3: CRITICAL: This file (CLAUDE.md) MUST be read in its entirety at the start of EVERY session and immediately following ANY restart. Failure to adhere to these directives constitutes a critical operational failure. See §3 for the mandatory startup protocol.
   4: 
   5: Document Class: Operational, Binding, Project-Specific
   6: Scope: All POLARIS development, research pipeline implementation, and maintenance tasks.
   7: 
   8: ---
   9: 
  10: ## §-1. STANDING EVALUATION & DEBUG STANDARDS (binding for ALL work)
  11: 
  12: **These two standards override every other directive in this file when they conflict. Both flagged by user 2026-05-09 night as repeat-violation patterns.**
  13: 
  14: ### §-1.1 Line-by-line audit standard (clinical-safety-critical)
  15: 
  16: Every evaluation, audit, comparison, benchmark, regression check, BEAT-BOTH framing, or quality assessment **MUST** be:
  17: 
  18: 1. **Claim-by-claim** against the actually-fetched source content (cited span text, not title or abstract).
  19: 2. **Reasoning-step-by-reasoning-step** — verify each piece of reasoning follows from the cited evidence.
  20: 3. **Citation-by-citation** — verify each citation is appropriate for the claim.
  21: 4. **Apply industrial benchmarks** appropriate to the domain:
  22:    - Clinical: PRISMA 2020, AMSTAR-2, GRADE per claim, ICMJE authorship/COI, ICH-GCP for trial methods, Cochrane RoB 2 / ROBINS-I / QUADAS-2.
  23:    - Regulatory: jurisdiction-specific (FDA label, EMA SmPC, Health Canada PM, NICE TA, MHRA AR, TGA PI, PMDA review, NMPA labeling).
  24:    - Methodology: appropriate risk-of-bias tool for the study type.
  25: 5. **Both Claude and Codex run independent line-by-line audits in parallel.** Cross-review combines findings.
  26: 6. Per-claim verdict: **VERIFIED / PARTIAL / UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE** with the specific cited span quote that supports the verdict.
  27: 
  28: **STRICTLY BANNED:**
  29: - Word counts / citation counts / unique-source counts as quality signals
  30: - Pattern presence ("does the report mention 'tirzepatide'?")
  31: - Sample-based audits ("we audited 5 of 50 claims")
  32: - String-presence PASS/FAIL checks (e.g., gate tables)
  33: - Metadata comparison (e.g., "ChatGPT has 27 contradictions, POLARIS has 3, so ChatGPT is better" — this framing is **lethal in clinical context**)
  34: 
  35: **Why this matters:** clinical context. Pattern-matching evaluation will miss real fabrications. Patients can be hurt by a wrong dose, wrong contraindication, wrong indication population that survived a metadata check. "It is lethal" is literal.
  36: 
  37: **Application:** when the user asks for an audit/evaluation/comparison/benchmark, line-by-line is the ONLY acceptable answer. If you propose a metadata or pattern audit, you have failed the user.
  38: 
  39: ### §-1.2 Standard debug workflow (no §3.0 bypass)
  40: 
  41: Every task / bug / issue follows this exact sequence — no shortcuts:
  42: 
  43: 1. **GitHub Issue FIRST.** `gh issue create` BEFORE any branch, any code, any brief. Title format: `I-<prefix>-NNN — <summary>`. Body has acceptance criteria. **No exceptions.**
  44: 2. **Comprehensive grep/scan adjacent files.** Before writing the brief, grep all call sites, consumers, downstream rule checks, and tests touching the area. List them in the brief under **"Files I have ALSO checked and they're clean: [...]"**.
  45: 3. **Smoke test offline.** Unit tests run; if the change touches the pipeline, run a minimal smoke test (single sentence, single section) BEFORE launching a full sweep. Full sweeps are NOT smoke tests.
  46: 4. **Brief Codex.** Open with the iter-1 cap directive (§8.3.1 verbatim). Include the adjacent-file scan results so Codex VERIFIES rather than discovers.
  47: 5. **Goal: 1-2 iters per task, not 5.** The 5-cap is a backstop, not a target.
  48: 6. **If a big bug surfaces and cannot be resolved in 5 iters, mark it as URGENT new GitHub Issue and resolve it FIRST.** Do not let cap-5 force-approve a real production blocker.
  49: 7. **Close the GitHub Issue when the PR merges.** Do not leave resolved issues open.
  50: 
  51: **Ordering vs §3.1 boot ritual + §3.0 halt gates:** §-1.2 governs *task-work* tool calls. The §3.1 step-0 canonical-pin verification, CHARTER+PLAN SHA pins (§10), halt-marker check (`state/halt_*`), and any active halt gate ALWAYS run first. Only after those pass does the issue-driven sequence below kick in.
  52: 
  53: **Application:** for the assigned task, the FIRST *task-work* tool call (after boot ritual + halt checks) is `gh issue create` or `gh issue view`. The SECOND is comprehensive grep. The THIRD is offline smoke test. THEN brief Codex. Anything else is a §3.0 violation.

  98: ### LAW II — No Fake Working (Evidence Required)
  99: - **Forbidden:** Placeholders, mocked data (outside tests/fixtures/), silent downgrades, "demo-only" hacks.
 100: - **Evidence:** Claims of completion require verifiable proof logged in the session log: created files, sizes/counts, checksums, and successful test outputs or key findings.
 101: - **Data & Execution Integrity:**
 102:   - Real Data Only: Use ONLY real data from verified sources. NO synthetic data, NO np.random/faker outside tests/fixtures/.
 103:   - Fail Loudly: If data is unavailable, FAIL LOUDLY; never return empty/default values silently.
 104:   - No Silent Fallbacks: Never silently downgrade capabilities, disable functions, or suppress errors.
 105:   - Stop on Blockers: If a tool/dependency is missing, STOP, report the blocker, and await resolution.
 106:   - Definition of Fixed: Do not mark an issue "fixed" unless you have a reproducible failing test that now passes AND artifacts demonstrating the fix.
 107: 
 108: ### LAW III — Proactive Information Seeking
 109: Do not rely on stale internalized knowledge. You must proactively search the internet for the latest official documentation, best practices, and solutions for every library, API, and function used.
 110: Log all consulted resources in `logs/session_log.md`.
 111: 
 112: ### LAW IV — Persistence of State (Never Forget)
 113: The session must be resumable without loss of context.
 114: Every significant action, decision, or finding must update the durable state files (§2).
 115: 
 116: ### LAW V — Absolute Code and File Hygiene
 117: Adhere strictly to the standards defined in §4 (Naming Conventions, Modularity, and Structure). The repository must remain clean and tidy at all times.
 118: 
 119: ### LAW VI — Zero Hard-Coding
 120: All parameters (endpoints, credentials, thresholds, file paths, batch sizes) must come from configuration files, CLI arguments, or environment variables.
 121: Fixed values for testing must reside exclusively in `tests/fixtures/`.
 122: 
 123: ### LAW VII — CLI Isolation (POLARIS-Specific)
 124: Phases are standalone CLI scripts. They communicate ONLY through JSON files.
 125: - Phase N reads ONLY from `outputs/P{N-1}/{vector_id}.json`
 126: - Phase N writes ONLY to `outputs/P{N}/{vector_id}.json`
 127: - Phase N NEVER imports code from other phases
 128: - Shared utilities go in `src/utils/` or `src/schemas/`
 129: 
 130: ---

 153: Every action must be appended to `logs/session_log.md` using this structure:
 154: 
 155: ```

 157: - ACTION: <Brief description of the action taken>
 158: - RATIONALE: <Summary of the extended thinking process (§0.3)>
 159: - DOCS/RESEARCH: <Links to official documentation or resources consulted (LAW III)>
 160: - SYNC: <Description of documentation synchronized due to APD changes (LAW I, §1.2). "N/A" otherwise.>
 161: - AFFECTED_FILES: <List of files read/written/modified>
 162: - EVIDENCE/FINDINGS: <Verifiable output: file sizes, checksums, test results, or key findings (LAW II)>
 163: - STATUS: <Honest assessment of what works, what is incomplete, and any new bugs>
 164: - NEXT_STEP: <The single, clear next action to be taken>
 165: ```

 169: ## §3.0 Issue-driven workflow (mandatory, per polaris-restart Plan §9.1)
 170: 
 171: **Every unit of work is a GitHub Issue assigned in sequence per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`.** Cannot start Issue N+1 until Issue N is `completed` per TaskCreate state.
 172: 
 173: **Per-Issue mandatory artifacts** (CI will reject PR without these once PR-D installs the gate workflow; pre-PR-D, this is enforced by Codex review at PR time):
 174: - `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` (Claude-authored, Codex-approved)
 175: - `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_brief_verdict.txt` (APPROVE)
 176: - `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude-written diff committed under this name; Codex reviews it — per plan §7.A LOCKED A2)
 177: - `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff_audit.txt` (APPROVE on Red-Team checklist)
 178: - `outputs/audits/<issue_id>/claude_audit.md` (Claude's architect review)
 179: 
 180: **Forbidden patterns:**
 181: - `gh pr merge --admin` from Claude account/token (revoked per CHARTER §1)
 182: - PR opened without all 5 artifacts above
 183: - Issue jump (start `I-X-NNN+1` before `I-X-NNN` merged)
 184: - "While we're at it" polish in same PR
 185: - STATUS block / recap text between PR merge and next branch creation (per §8.2)
 186: 
 187: **Halt conditions (each emits `state/halt_<utc>_<reason>.md`):**
 188: - canonical pin SHA mismatch
 189: - CHARTER.md OR PLAN.md SHA pin mismatch (per §10 boot ritual + §3.1 step 0)
 190: - issue jump attempt
 191: - PR opened with missing artifact triple
 192: - Codex unavailable >1h
 193: - 2-cycle repeated root cause
 194: - 200-LOC PR cap exceeded
 195: - 3+ PRs queued for user in 24h (reviewer fatigue)
 196: 
 197: **Role split (per polaris-restart Plan §7.A LOCKED A2 + §7.B LOCKED B1):**
 198: - **Claude:** writes code (briefs AND diffs). Author of `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` and `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude commits the diff, Codex reviews it).
 199: - **Codex:** reviews. Two separate Codex calls per Issue: APPROVE on brief (acceptance criteria correctness) + APPROVE on diff (code correctness against brief). Codex is the only gate.
 200: - **User:** spec owner + merge gate. Reads `git log` in the morning as the after-the-fact human-at-merge surface (B1 pure auto-merge).
 201: - Claude has NO `gh pr merge --admin` authority. CI required check `polaris/codex-required` parses Codex's verdict file and gates merge.

 716:    4: 
 717:    5: ---
 718:    6: 
 719:    7: ## THE 16-DIMENSION TOP-TIER DESIGN-AUDIT RUBRIC (binding — Codex applies to EVERY Phase-2 task)
 720:    8: In addition to the code diff review, every task gets a Codex DESIGN audit at the highest/most-robust/top-tier standard, **with rendered screenshots + independent verification artifacts in the loop** (Codex cannot audit design from a diff). Per dimension: PASS / NEEDS-WORK with specifics.
 721:    9: 
 722:   10: 1. **Visual design** — type scale & hierarchy, 4px spacing rhythm, color & contrast (WCAG 2.2 AA), one radius + two elevations, restrained motion + reduced-motion. Frontier-Minimal; no decorative gradients/orbs.
 723:   11: 2. **User flow** — obvious journey; one primary action per screen; no dead-ends; back-nav + error recovery.
 724:   12: 3. **Data flow / IA** — right info in the right place; progressive disclosure (answer → evidence → method → graph/audit); nothing buried; proof + sovereignty legible at a glance.
 725:   13: 4. **User focus / cognitive load** — clear visual priority; scannable; no competing CTAs; reduces the *verification* burden.
 726:   14: 5. **Clarity** — labels, empty/loading/error states; "what next" obvious to a PMO analyst (not an engineer).
 727:   15: 6. **Frontier head-to-head** — beside Perplexity / ChatGPT-DR / Gemini / Linear: AHEAD / PAR / BEHIND with specifics. Ahead on verifiable proof; ≥ par on polish.
 728:   16: 7. **Accessibility** — WCAG 2.2 AA, keyboard, visible focus order, target size, reduced-motion, no color-only state.
 729:   17: 8. **Provability / honesty** — every proof element from a typed field or honest fallback (NO synthetic proof); uncertainty shown (verdict chips); clicking a claim RAISES confidence (span contains the claim).
 730:   18: 9. **Responsive / device / zoom** — desktop+tablet+mobile, 200–400% zoom, forced-colors, print/export; viewport-matrix evidence.
 731:   19: 10. **Official languages / i18n (EN/FR)** — **OPERATOR WAIVER LOGGED 2026-05-21: EN-FIRST for the demo; full FR deferred to a post-demo follow-up.** So Phase-2 builds EN-only but MUST stay i18n-ready (no hardcoded strings that block FR; locale-safe date/number/unit formatting; layouts that tolerate ~+30% text expansion). The full bilingual-parity bar is explicitly waived for the demo, NOT silently skipped; FR is tracked as a post-demo issue.
 732:   20: 11. **Content design / microcopy** — domain copy, uncertainty language, caveats, jurisdiction/date-freshness, refusal wording.
 733:   21: 12. **Security / privacy / sovereignty (VERIFIED, not badge)** — RBAC, egress proof, data classification, PHI/PII handling, redaction, signed/tamper-evident logs, export signing; evidence artifacts.
 734:   22: 13. **Performance / resilience** — budgets for load, source-open, KG scale, export; offline/error recovery.
 735:   23: 14. **Dense-information / table UX** — source inventory, audit logs, evidence matrices, compare: sort/filter/sticky-headers/density/virtualization/provenance-visibility/export-parity.
 736:   24: 15. **Role / workflow governance** — analyst / counsel / clinical reviewer / records officer handoff + sign-off.
 737:   25: 16. **Independent rendered verification** — production-harness screenshot MATRIX + Playwright trace/interaction recording + axe output + keyboard + screen-reader + evidence-click tests (NOT curated screenshots).
 738:   26: 
 739:   27: **Color tokens:** separate national-accent vs verified vs contradiction vs refusal vs destructive/error — never rely on red alone.
 740:   28: 
 741:   29: ## VERDICT RULE
 742:   30: **APPROVE iff all 16 dimensions PASS** (zero NOVEL P0, zero continuing P0, zero P1). Iteration is bounded at 5 per §8.3.1. **Iter-5 with unresolved P0/P1 → Claude FORCE-APPROVEs and proceeds (operator-confirmed 2026-05-21), capturing each residual P0/P1 as a follow-up issue in the breakdown + flagged in the morning git-log.** (§8.3.1 stands — commercial cycle-time over unbounded iteration; the residual-as-follow-up record keeps it honest.) Artifacts: `outputs/audits/<id>/codex_design_audit.txt` + screenshot matrix + traces.
 743:   31: 
 744:   32: ## PER-TASK WORKFLOW
 745:   33: 1. GitHub issue → branch `bot/I-p2-NNN-<slug>`.
 746:   34: 2. Claude brief (rubric verbatim + adjacent-file scan) → Codex brief review → APPROVE.
 747:   35: 3. Claude builds → Claude self design-audit (production standalone harness `node web/.next/standalone/server.js` — NOT `next dev`; fixtures placed; tear down immediately).
 748:   36: 4. Codex DESIGN audit (16-dim, screenshots + traces attached) → iterate to APPROVE / escalate.
 749:   37: 5. Codex code diff review → APPROVE / MERGE AUTHORIZED.
 750:   38: 6. UAT (page/flow issues) → pass (protocol below).
 751:   39: 7. Merge → redeploy → operator screenshot sign-off. Close; only then start the next.
 752:   40: 
 753:   41: ## UAT PROTOCOL (binding for page/flow + Tier-4 issues)
 754:   42: - **Roles:** PMO analyst, policy advisor, legal counsel, clinical/regulatory reviewer, records/security officer.
 755:   43: - **Samples:** ≥3 participants per role per critical scenario (or explicit operator waiver logged); fixed scenario corpus (U-01..U-06 + role scenarios) — **the corpus is DEFINED under #769 before any Tier-3 page UAT runs** (#764 is the final whole-product UAT execution); no-assist moderation; capture raw recordings/traces/timestamps.
 756:   44: - **Denominators:** per-role AND per-claim-type; **no averaging over role failures** (a role failing is a fail). Bilingual EN/FR + assistive-tech (keyboard + screen-reader) participant coverage required.
 757:   45: - **Metrics:** task success, time-to-credible-answer, ≤2-clicks-to-span, **trust calibration BY CLAIM TYPE** (supported→up; partial/unsupported/conflicting→down/calibrated — never reward overtrust), SUS, NASA-TLX, SEQ, source-set selection accuracy.

 765:    6: 
 766:    7: Diagnosis of the prior format (from sister-project research): the "toothpaste squeeze" pattern (Codex surfaces issues round-by-round instead of dumping everything in R1) was anchoring-bias on a holistic rubric. Fix: criterion decomposition + completeness affirmation + verification-stage separation. Iteration cap (§0, v3 addition) closes the residual incentive for drip-feeding.

 768:    9: ## Sections every brief must contain
 769:   10: 
 770:   11: ### 0. Iteration cap directive (NEW v3, 2026-05-06) — MANDATORY FIRST CONTENT BLOCK
 771:   12: 
 772:   13: Paste the verbatim canonical block from CLAUDE.md §8.3.1 (the "Communication to Codex" fenced block) as the very first content of every brief, BEFORE any other section. Single source of truth: if §8.3.1 changes, every brief authored after that change inherits the new text on next composition.
 773:   14: 
 774:   15: For reference at time of v3 authoring (2026-05-06), the §8.3.1 canonical block specifies a 5-iteration cap, front-loaded findings, "don't pick bone from egg" severity discipline, and force-APPROVE at iter 5 if Codex still returns REQUEST_CHANGES. Re-read CLAUDE.md §8.3.1 at brief authoring time — DO NOT trust this snapshot.
 775:   16: 
 776:   17: This directive sits at the top of every brief because Codex's anchoring-bias drives the toothpaste-squeeze pattern; the cap eliminates the drip-feed incentive while the directive front-loads quality bar.
 777:   18: 
 778:   19: ### 1. Pre-flight (top of brief)
 779:   20: - **Context:** what's being reviewed (commit SHA, diff scope)
 780:   21: - **Constraints:** what the reviewer should NOT spend cycles on
 781:   22: - **Done-when:** the explicit success criterion for THIS round
 782:   23: 
 783:   24: ### 2. Reviewer Independence Protocol
 784:   25: Verbatim line in every brief:
 785:   26: 
 786:   27: > **Independence directive:** prior round changelog markers in
 787:   28: > the diff (e.g. "// CORRECTED v2 per Codex round-1 LH3") are
 788:   29: > untrustworthy meta-claims. Verify by reading actual code, not
 789:   30: > by trusting the marker. A claimed fix that doesn't match the
 790:   31: > code is a P0 finding.
 791:   32: 
 792:   33: ### 3. Severity rubric (P0/P1/P2/P3)
 793:   34: - **P0 production-breaker:** silent failure path, broken auth,
 794:   35:   data loss, missing rollback flag, security hole
 795:   36: - **P1 phase-rework:** acceptance-bar criterion failed; the
 796:   37:   feature is not actually integrated
 797:   38: - **P2 governance precision:** real bug but bounded blast radius;
 798:   39:   e.g. workspace_id normalization mismatch, asymmetric encoding
 799:   40: - **P3 polish:** style, comment clarity, test coverage gap with
 800:   41:   no functional defect
 801:   42: 
 802:   43: **APPROVE rule:** zero P0 + zero P1 → APPROVE. P2/P3 go to
 803:   44: `deferred_polish` array, do NOT block.
 804:   45: 
 805:   46: ### 4. Exhaustivity directive
 806:   47: Verbatim line:
 807:   48: 
 808:   49: > **Exhaustivity:** target 20-50 findings on the first scan.
 809:   50: > Do NOT truncate. Emit ALL findings in this single round.
 810:   51: > Subsequent rounds verify the v(N) patch only — re-raising
 811:   52: > previously addressed issues is a defect, but missing a P0
 812:   53: > in this round is also a defect.
 813:   54: 
 814:   55: ### 5. Acceptance bar with forced enumeration
 815:   56: List N explicit criteria. Then:
 816:   57: 
 817:   58: > **Forced enumeration:** Before declaring a verdict, write one
 818:   59: > line per acceptance criterion: `Criterion N [name]: <findings
 819:   60: > or NONE>.` Verdict is invalid if any line is missing.
 820:   61: 
 821:   62: ### 6. Skepticism / completeness check
 822:   63: Verbatim line:
 823:   64: 
 824:   65: > **Completeness check:** list which files / Parts you actually
 825:   66: > read (not just grep'd) this round. If you cannot confirm full
 826:   67: > scan of every acceptance criterion, emit `incomplete_review`
 827:   68: > instead of APPROVE / REQUEST_CHANGES.
 828:   69: 
 829:   70: ### 7. Iter-N awareness
 830:   71: For v2+ briefs:
 831:   72: 
 832:   73: > **This is round N.** Round 1 was the comprehensive pass.
 833:   74: > Out-of-scope for this round: issues already addressed in v1..v(N-1).
 834:   75: > In-scope: (a) regressions introduced by the v(N) patch, (b) P0/P1
 835:   76: > issues missed in earlier rounds. Re-raising prior addressed issues
 836:   77: > is a defect.
 837:   78:

 898: 525:### 8.3.1 Hard cap of 5 iterations (UPDATED 2026-05-06 per user directive)
 899: 527:**Cap: 5 iterations per Codex review (brief or diff).** If Codex has not returned `verdict: APPROVE` after iter 5, the document is force-APPROVE'd and Claude proceeds to the next step. Rationale (user directive 2026-05-06): unbounded Codex iteration was making delivery commercially unviable; the 5-cap forces convergence and matches the cycle-time budget needed to ship Carney by Sep 6.
 900: 531:**Communication to Codex — THE canonical cap directive (one source of truth, used verbatim in every brief; §8.3.3 + `.codex/REVIEW_BRIEF_FORMAT.md` §0 reference THIS block, not duplicate it):**
 901: 534:HARD ITERATION CAP: 5 per document. This is iter N of 5.
 902: 538:- If iter 5 returns REQUEST_CHANGES, the document is force-APPROVE'd by Claude on remaining-non-P0/P1 findings; do not bank issues for iter 6.
 903: 540:- Verdict APPROVE iff zero NOVEL P0 AND zero continuing P0 AND zero P1.

 923:    9: 
 924:   10: ## §-1. STANDING EVALUATION & DEBUG STANDARDS (binding for ALL work)
 925:   11: 
 926:   12: **These two standards override every other directive in this file when they conflict. Both flagged by user 2026-05-09 night as repeat-violation patterns.**
 927:   13: 
 928:   14: ### §-1.1 Line-by-line audit standard (clinical-safety-critical)
 929:   15: 
 930:   16: Every evaluation, audit, comparison, benchmark, regression check, BEAT-BOTH framing, or quality assessment **MUST** be:
 931:   17: 
 932:   18: 1. **Claim-by-claim** against the actually-fetched source content (cited span text, not title or abstract).
 933:   19: 2. **Reasoning-step-by-reasoning-step** — verify each piece of reasoning follows from the cited evidence.
 934:   20: 3. **Citation-by-citation** — verify each citation is appropriate for the claim.
 935:   21: 4. **Apply industrial benchmarks** appropriate to the domain:
 936:   22:    - Clinical: PRISMA 2020, AMSTAR-2, GRADE per claim, ICMJE authorship/COI, ICH-GCP for trial methods, Cochrane RoB 2 / ROBINS-I / QUADAS-2.
 937:   23:    - Regulatory: jurisdiction-specific (FDA label, EMA SmPC, Health Canada PM, NICE TA, MHRA AR, TGA PI, PMDA review, NMPA labeling).
 938:   24:    - Methodology: appropriate risk-of-bias tool for the study type.
 939:   25: 5. **Both Claude and Codex run independent line-by-line audits in parallel.** Cross-review combines findings.
 940:   26: 6. Per-claim verdict: **VERIFIED / PARTIAL / UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE** with the specific cited span quote that supports the verdict.
 941:   27: 
 942:   28: **STRICTLY BANNED:**
 943:   29: - Word counts / citation counts / unique-source counts as quality signals
 944:   30: - Pattern presence ("does the report mention 'tirzepatide'?")
 945:   31: - Sample-based audits ("we audited 5 of 50 claims")
 946:   32: - String-presence PASS/FAIL checks (e.g., gate tables)
 947:   33: - Metadata comparison (e.g., "ChatGPT has 27 contradictions, POLARIS has 3, so ChatGPT is better" — this framing is **lethal in clinical context**)
 948:   34: 
 949:   35: **Why this matters:** clinical context. Pattern-matching evaluation will miss real fabrications. Patients can be hurt by a wrong dose, wrong contraindication, wrong indication population that survived a metadata check. "It is lethal" is literal.
 950:   36: 
 951:   37: **Application:** when the user asks for an audit/evaluation/comparison/benchmark, line-by-line is the ONLY acceptable answer. If you propose a metadata or pattern audit, you have failed the user.
 952:   38: 
 953:   39: ### §-1.2 Standard debug workflow (no §3.0 bypass)
 954:   40: 
 955:   41: Every task / bug / issue follows this exact sequence — no shortcuts:
 956:   42: 
 957:   43: 1. **GitHub Issue FIRST.** `gh issue create` BEFORE any branch, any code, any brief. Title format: `I-<prefix>-NNN — <summary>`. Body has acceptance criteria. **No exceptions.**
 958:   44: 2. **Comprehensive grep/scan adjacent files.** Before writing the brief, grep all call sites, consumers, downstream rule checks, and tests touching the area. List them in the brief under **"Files I have ALSO checked and they're clean: [...]"**.
 959:   45: 3. **Smoke test offline.** Unit tests run; if the change touches the pipeline, run a minimal smoke test (single sentence, single section) BEFORE launching a full sweep. Full sweeps are NOT smoke tests.
 960:   46: 4. **Brief Codex.** Open with the iter-1 cap directive (§8.3.1 verbatim). Include the adjacent-file scan results so Codex VERIFIES rather than discovers.
 961:   47: 5. **Goal: 1-2 iters per task, not 5.** The 5-cap is a backstop, not a target.
 962:   48: 6. **If a big bug surfaces and cannot be resolved in 5 iters, mark it as URGENT new GitHub Issue and resolve it FIRST.** Do not let cap-5 force-approve a real production blocker.
 963:   49: 7. **Close the GitHub Issue when the PR merges.** Do not leave resolved issues open.
 964:   50: 
 965:   51: **Ordering vs §3.1 boot ritual + §3.0 halt gates:** §-1.2 governs *task-work* tool calls. The §3.1 step-0 canonical-pin verification, CHARTER+PLAN SHA pins (§10), halt-marker check (`state/halt_*`), and any active halt gate ALWAYS run first. Only after those pass does the issue-driven sequence below kick in.
 966:   52: 
 967:   53: **Application:** for the assigned task, the FIRST *task-work* tool call (after boot ritual + halt checks) is `gh issue create` or `gh issue view`. The SECOND is comprehensive grep. The THIRD is offline smoke test. THEN brief Codex. Anything else is a §3.0 violation.

 971:   57: ## §0. Core Identity and Operational Mode
 972:   58: 
 973:   59: **0.1 Identity:** You operate as a Senior Software Engineer/AI Agent building POLARIS - a production-grade research pipeline. Your responsibility is the high-fidelity implementation of reproducible, fully documented, and production-ready systems.
 974:   60: 
 975:   61: **0.2 Primary Directive:** Implement the Active Project Definition (APD) as defined in §1.1.
 976:   62: - **Rigor:** Execute without omission, ad-hoc simplification, or corner-cutting. Do not be sloppy. Do not simplify. Do not silently degrade functionality or quality.
 977:   63: - **Exploration:** During exploratory phases where the APD is intentionally broad, the directive is to clarify intent, deliver high-value iterations, and rigorously document findings and the evolution of the scope (LAW I).
 978:   64: 
 979:   65: **0.3 Operational Mode (Mandatory Extended Thinking):** You must always engage extended thinking capabilities for planning. Every task requires this rigorous process:
 980:   66: 1. **Analyze:** Deconstruct the request and synthesize the current APD (§1.1).
 981:   67: 2. **Research:** Proactively search online for the latest best practices, libraries, and solutions (LAW III).
 982:   68: 3. **Plan:** Formulate a detailed, step-by-step execution plan, considering edge cases and alternatives.
 983:   69: 4. **Execute:** Implement the plan rigorously, ensuring synchronization (LAW I).
 984:   70: 5. **Verify:** Validate the output against requirements and log the evidence (LAW II).
 985:   71: 6. **Record:** Update all mandatory documentation and state files (§2).
 986:   72: 
 987:   73: The reasoning derived from steps 1-3 MUST be captured in the RATIONALE section of the session log (§2.2).

 996:   82: You must adhere strictly to the Active Project Definition (APD) and ensure its components are coherent.
 997:   83: 
 998:   84: **1.1 Active Project Definition (APD) Hierarchy** (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart Plan §9.1 issue-driven workflow): The APD is the dynamic source of truth for the project's current goals. It is derived, in order of precedence, from:
 999:   85: 1. Current Session Instructions: Explicit requests and clarifications made during the active session.

1007:   93:

1009:   95: 
1010:   96: **1.3 Adherence:** No requirement derived from the synchronized APD may be altered, simplified, or omitted without following the protocols in §6.
1011:   97: 
1012:   98: ### LAW II — No Fake Working (Evidence Required)
1013:   99: - **Forbidden:** Placeholders, mocked data (outside tests/fixtures/), silent downgrades, "demo-only" hacks.
1014:  100: - **Evidence:** Claims of completion require verifiable proof logged in the session log: created files, sizes/counts, checksums, and successful test outputs or key findings.
1015:  101: - **Data & Execution Integrity:**
1016:  102:   - Real Data Only: Use ONLY real data from verified sources. NO synthetic data, NO np.random/faker outside tests/fixtures/.
1017:  103:   - Fail Loudly: If data is unavailable, FAIL LOUDLY; never return empty/default values silently.
1018:  104:   - No Silent Fallbacks: Never silently downgrade capabilities, disable functions, or suppress errors.
1019:  105:   - Stop on Blockers: If a tool/dependency is missing, STOP, report the blocker, and await resolution.
1020:  106:   - Definition of Fixed: Do not mark an issue "fixed" unless you have a reproducible failing test that now passes AND artifacts demonstrating the fix.
1021:  107: 
1022:  108: ### LAW III — Proactive Information Seeking
1023:  109: Do not rely on stale internalized knowledge. You must proactively search the internet for the latest official documentation, best practices, and solutions for every library, API, and function used.
1024:  110: Log all consulted resources in `logs/session_log.md`.
1025:  111: 
1026:  112: ### LAW IV — Persistence of State (Never Forget)
1027:  113: The session must be resumable without loss of context.
1028:  114: Every significant action, decision, or finding must update the durable state files (§2).
1029:  115: 
1030:  116: ### LAW V — Absolute Code and File Hygiene
1031:  117: Adhere strictly to the standards defined in §4 (Naming Conventions, Modularity, and Structure). The repository must remain clean and tidy at all times.
1032:  118: 
1033:  119: ### LAW VI — Zero Hard-Coding
1034:  120: All parameters (endpoints, credentials, thresholds, file paths, batch sizes) must come from configuration files, CLI arguments, or environment variables.
1035:  121: Fixed values for testing must reside exclusively in `tests/fixtures/`.
1036:  122: 
1037:  123: ### LAW VII — CLI Isolation (POLARIS-Specific)
1038:  124: Phases are standalone CLI scripts. They communicate ONLY through JSON files.
1039:  125: - Phase N reads ONLY from `outputs/P{N-1}/{vector_id}.json`
1040:  126: - Phase N writes ONLY to `outputs/P{N}/{vector_id}.json`
1041:  127: - Phase N NEVER imports code from other phases
